    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="22af007386a145afb0e01430fd35b9a6">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: 'a323ec97-5f01-4b6d-89f1-2cb27094906c'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

   <div class="abstract-group  metis-abstract">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d62918576" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Alloy-type materials are desirable for high-energy sodium-ion batteries. Different from nanoengineering with pre-reserving void space and confined carbon coatings, microsized particles promise high specific/volumetric capacities, easy manufacturing, and low cost but are prone to rapid capacity loss. Herein, inspired by the process of “root growth in soil”, microsized Bi particles (µm-Bi, as “seeds”) surrounded by microsized hard carbon particles (µm-HC, as “soil”) are ingeniously dispersed through a simple mixing approach. This design utilizes the morphological self-evolution of µm-Bi into Bi-nanonetworks between dispersed µm-HC during repeated (de)sodiations, leading to a stable capacity retention of 99.8% for 2000 cycles, higher than that of the µm-Bi electrode (7.2%) at a high mass loading of 5.5 mg cm<sup>−2</sup>. The interconnected Bi-nanonetworks and µm-HC particles provide continuous electron pathways and facilitate electrolyte infiltration, which effectively boosts electrical contact, stable cycling, and high-rate capability. Especially, the hybrid Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> (optimized weight ratio) thick-film electrode shows boosted comprehensive electrochemical performance, superior to HC and µm-Bi electrodes. The Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> full cell, assembled without any pre-treatment, delivers 4500 stable cycles. This nature-inspired strategy provides a simple yet practical approach for employing the electrochemically driven evolution of micro-sized active materials and realizing high specific/volumetric capacities, fast kinetics, and long-term cycling stability.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202412636-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202412636-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>As an alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale renewable energy storage in grids, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are being commercialized owing to the high abundance, worldwide distribution, and low cost of sodium resources.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0001_R_d62918568e530" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nat. Rev. Mater.">1</a>-<a href="#adma202412636-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0004_R_d62918568e530" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nat. Energy">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Compared to those of LIBs, the industrial applications of SIBs are considered to balance specific/volumetric energy densities, rate capabilities, life spans, and costs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0005_R_d62918568e535" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Nat. Rev. Mater.">5</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0006_R_d62918568e535" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Chem. Rev.">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Layered transition metal oxides, phosphates, and Prussian blue analogs have been well developed as cathode materials for reversible (de)intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> ions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0007_R_d62918568e543" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the low-cost graphite anode delivers limited sodium-ion storage capacity owing to the non-embeddability of Na<sup>+</sup> in the graphite layers.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0001_R_d62918568e550" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nat. Rev. Mater.">1</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0008_R_d62918568e550" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In this respect, the significant challenges of advanced SIBs rely on developing anode materials with comprehensive electrochemical performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0009_R_d62918568e556" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Energy Environ. Sci">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Hard carbon (HC) anodes, composed of randomly stacked defective graphene nanosheets with large interlayer distances and rich closed pores, are able to accommodate Na<sup>+</sup> ions with a specific capacity above 300 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and long-term cycling stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0010_R_d62918568e567" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Energy Mater.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, HC anodes face several limitations, such as low compaction density (≈1.0 g cm<sup>−3</sup>), low volumetric capacity, and poor rate capability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0011_R_d62918568e575" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">11</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0012_R_d62918568e575" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Adv. Mater.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Alloying-type anodes, e.g., Bi, Sn, Pb, and Sb, exhibit high theoretical specific and volumetric capacities. Among them, Bi undergoes reversible two-step alloying reactions of Bi↔NaBi↔Na<sub>3</sub>Bi, resulting in high theoretical specific and volumetric capacities of 385 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and 3800 mAh cm<sup>−3</sup> (the density of Bi is 9.2 g cm<sup>−3</sup>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0013_R_d62918568e589" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Energy Storage Mater.">13</a>-<a href="#adma202412636-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0015_R_d62918568e589" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - J. Mater. Chem. A">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In particular, the formed <i>h</i>-Na<sub>3</sub>Bi is a 3D-topological Dirac semimetal (regarded as “3D graphene”), displaying higher electrical conductivity and Na<sup>+</sup> diffusivity than those of Na-Sn and Na-Pb alloys.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0016_R_d62918568e601" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Science">16</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0017_R_d62918568e601" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These novel properties of Na-Bi alloys enable their excellent high-rate capabilities.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0018_R_d62918568e606" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Adv. Mater.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, Bi anodes suffer from a large theoretical volume expansion of ≈244% during sodiation, leading to severe pulverization and agglomeration.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0013_R_d62918568e611" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Energy Storage Mater.">13</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0019_R_d62918568e611" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - J. Energy Chem">19</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0020_R_d62918568e611" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Energy Environ. Sci">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During repeated volume changes, the fragmentized active materials easily lose electrical contact and detach from the current collector, leading to rapid capacity fading.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0021_R_d62918568e617" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Nat. Energy">21</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0022_R_d62918568e617" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Nature">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Many strategies have been proposed to overcome the fast capacity fading of alloy-type materials, including the commonly known nanostructural engineering, hybrid nanocomposites, and electrolyte optimization.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0013_R_d62918568e624" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Energy Storage Mater.">13</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0017_R_d62918568e624" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">17</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0023_R_d62918568e624" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Appl. Surface Sci.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Embedding the Bi nanoparticles into a confined carbon-coating structure has been widely designed, such as Bi nanoparticle@carbon,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0024_R_d62918568e629" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Mater.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Bi@void@C nanospheres,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0025_R_d62918568e634" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Nano Lett.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and Bi nanospheres@C⊂CFs<sup>26</sup>, which provide buffering spaces for volume expansion and displays stable cycles. However, these Bi nanocomposites delivered the initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) below 80.0% (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0019_R_d62918568e645" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - J. Energy Chem">19</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0020_R_d62918568e645" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Energy Environ. Sci">20</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0024_R_d62918568e645" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Mater.">24</a>-<a href="#adma202412636-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0031_R_d62918568e645" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, the complex synthesis processes of nanomaterials increase manufacturing costs, which hid the advantage of using low-cost Bi metal (≈9 k$ per ton).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0032_R_d62918568e651" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These adverse effects of nanostructured Bi@C composites limit their large-scale applications.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0033_R_d62918568e656" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Nat. Energy">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Recently, micro-sized Bi (µm-Bi) particles anode (at a mass loading of 3.0 mg cm<sup>−2</sup>) displayed promising sodium-ion storage performance in ether-based electrolytes, delivering a high ICE of 94.8%, capacity retention of 94.4% after 2000 cycles at 0.4 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and high-rate capability of 356 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 2.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0031_R_d62918568e670" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Through spontaneous disordered fragmentation and reaggregation processes during cycling, the µm-Bi gradually evolved into 3D porous Bi-nanonetworks, which enhanced Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion and structural stability after subsequent cycling. Nevertheless, most of the electrochemical performances of Bi and Bi/C nanocomposites have been reported for thin-film electrodes at mass loadings of only 1−3 mg cm<sup>−2</sup> (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0019_R_d62918568e683" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - J. Energy Chem">19</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0020_R_d62918568e683" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Energy Environ. Sci">20</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0024_R_d62918568e683" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Mater.">24</a>-<a href="#adma202412636-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0031_R_d62918568e683" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which is far away from practical applications in industrial SIBs requiring a single-side areal capacity of over 1.5 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0034_R_d62918568e690" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Energy Mater.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>In this work, we investigated the electrochemical performance of µm-Bi thick-film electrode at a single-side mass loading of ≈5.5 mg cm<sup>−2</sup> (a theoretical single-side areal capacity of 2.1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>), but it failed to exhibit stable cycling stability as the thin-film electrode. The rapid capacity fading arises from the electrothermally driven self-evolution of µm-Bi into 3D Bi-nanonetworks with large volume changes and loss of electrical contact. This process is very similar to the sprouting of “seeds” (µm-Bi) and the growth of their “roots” (Bi-nanonetworks) in water (liquid electrolyte). The rotten roots break away from the body (the Bi-nanonetwork detaches from current collectors), leading to a short lifespan. Inspired by the natural process of “root growth in soil”, where roots firmly grip soil with boosted structure stability, we ingeniously disperse the µm-Bi particles (“seeds”) surrounded by the µm-HC particles (“soils”) through a simple mixing approach. Different from the strategies of carbon-coated confinements,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0024_R_d62918568e701" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Mater.">24</a>-<a href="#adma202412636-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0027_R_d62918568e701" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> our µm-Bi/µm-HC is an open structural design that utilizes the self-evolution of microsized Bi during electrothermal (de)alloying reactions. Benefiting from this idea, the Bi<sub>40</sub>/HC<sub>60</sub> thick-film electrode (with an optimized ratio by weight) displays an areal capacity of 1.77 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, negligible capacity loss for 2000 cycles at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, a high ICE of 88.2%, high-rate capacities and high volumetric capacities. The as-assembled full cell of Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> delivers a high energy density of ≈141 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at a power density of 1546&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> for 4,500 stable cycles.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202412636-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202412636-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202412636-sec-0030">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adma202412636-sec-0030-title">2.1 Morphology Evolution and Rapid Capacity Fading of µm-Bi Thick-Film Electrode</h3>
            
            <p>The µm-Bi has a particle size of 5–10 µm (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). The in situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information) demonstrates the two-step alloying reaction from Bi to NaBi and then to <i>h</i>-Na<sub>3</sub>Bi.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0037_R_d62918568e758" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - J. Power Sources">37</a>-<a href="#adma202412636-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0039_R_d62918568e758" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Cell Rep. Phys. Sci.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In situ optical microscopy images (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>; Video <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information) reveal the rapid expansion of µm-Bi particles into irregular bumps with a large volume change of 118% for NaBi and 330% for Na<sub>3</sub>Bi. Such expansion is very uneven. In contrast to the excellent cycling stability of the thin-film electrode (at 2&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>), unfortunately, the µm-Bi thick-film electrode (at 5.5 mg cm<sup>−2</sup>) displays a capacity retention of only 16.6% after 1000 cycles (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0001">1a</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). Furthermore, high-rate capability is difficult to remain at thick-film electrodes (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202412636-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3167bf9e-e528-499d-8a62-66e59fb71d0c/adma202412636-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/3167bf9e-e528-499d-8a62-66e59fb71d0c/adma202412636-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/279d47fc-8b6b-47d2-abb4-e18df6a08dc5/adma202412636-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3167bf9e-e528-499d-8a62-66e59fb71d0c/adma202412636-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202412636-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202412636" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The cycling performance and morphology evolution of µm-Bi in liquid electrolytes. a) Cycling performance of the µm-Bi electrode at 2.0 and 5.5 mg cm<sup>−2</sup>. The thick-film µm-Bi electrode shows rapid capacity fading. b–k) Corresponding cross-sectional SEM images of the µm-Bi electrode b,c) at the pristine state, d,e) after 1 cycle, f,g) after 10 cycles, h,i) after 500 cycles, and j,k) after 1000 cycles, respectively. The µm-Bi turns into nanoparticles, nanonetworks, and then into coarsened networks during cycling.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The cross-sectional SEM images of the µm-Bi thick-film anode at different cycles are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0001">1b–k</a>. After 1 cycle, the pristine microsized Bi particles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0001">1b,c</a>) turn into inter-connected nanoparticles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0001">1d,e</a>) owing to the phase separation between Bi and Na<sub>3</sub>Bi accompanied by a large volume expansion. After 10 cycles, the sequential pulverization and reaggregation of the nanoparticles evolve into 3D porous nanonetworks (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0001">1f,g</a>), caused by the repeated phase separation process (spinodal decomposition) at the solid-electrolyte interface.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0035_R_d62918568e829" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Nature">35</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0036_R_d62918568e829" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Nat. Mater.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> After long-term cycling, the walls of the nanonetworks became coarsened (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0001">1h,i</a>). The detachment of Bi-nanonetworks from the current collector leads to a large capacity loss after 1000 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0001">1j,k</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202412636-sec-0040">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adma202412636-sec-0040-title">2.2 Root-Growth-Inspired Self-Evolution of µm-Bi whin µm-HC Matrix</h3>
            
            <p>The above morphological evolution of µm-Bi thick-film electrode cycled in liquid electrolyte is very similar to that of the “seed sprout and root growth in water” (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202412636-fig-0002">2a</a>). When the as-formed Bi-nanonetworks are detached from current collectors, the capacity rapidly fades. Different from “root growth in water”, the roots-soil structure has boosted stability, leading to a long lifespan. Inspired by the natural process of “root growth in soil” (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0002">2b</a>), the µm-Bi (“seeds”) and HC particles (“soil”, Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, Supporting Information) were well mixed by a low-speed ball-milling method, then making into thick-film electrode (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202412636-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/5fa44061-bee7-440e-8500-da05b60b636c/adma202412636-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/5fa44061-bee7-440e-8500-da05b60b636c/adma202412636-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/5f933f16-b264-4ffe-8492-c7db781cf5e6/adma202412636-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/5fa44061-bee7-440e-8500-da05b60b636c/adma202412636-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202412636-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202412636" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Root-growth-inspired design of the self-morphology-evolution of microsized bismuth surrounded by hard carbon. a) The morphology evolution of µm-Bi in liquid electrolyte is similar to “seeds sprout” and “roots growth” in water. The large volume expansion causes the detachment of Bi (“rotten roots”) from the current collector, leading to a short cycling lifespan. b) The morphological evolution of µm-Bi surrounded by µm-HC particles is similar to the “roots growth in soil”. The electrochemically formed 3D Bi-nanonetworks unitize the voids of staked HC particles, akin to the “roots grip the soil” with stable anchorage systems. The conductive Bi-nanonetworks@HC ensures continuous e<sup>−</sup> and ion transport.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>As a result, the hybrid Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> electrode displays stable 1000 cycles (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202412636-fig-0003">3a</a>) at 5.5 mg cm<sup>−2</sup>, which is much better than that of µm-Bi thick-film electrode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0001">1a</a>). Galvanostatic charge–discharge curves of Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> thick-film electrode at different cycles (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, Supporting Information) show no capacity loss from the Bi and HC reactions. The cross-sectional SEM images of Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0003">3b–k</a>) show the self-evolution of µm-Bi surrounded by the HC matrix at different cycles. After 1 cycle, µm-Bi (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0003">3b,c</a>) transforms into aggregated nanoparticles, which are surrounded by HC particles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0003">3d,e</a>). From 10 to 1000 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0003">3f–k</a>), the aggregated nanoparticles evolve into 3D porous Bi-nanonetworks. The Bi-nanonetworks are filled in the voids surrounded by HC particles, which is very similar to the robust “roots firmly grip the soil” structure (inset of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0002">2b</a>). Different from the evolution µm-Bi in a liquid electrolyte, in the µm-Bi/µm-HC hybrid structure, the porous 3D Bi-networks can expand and shrink between the voids, alleviating the total volume changes for repeated (de)alloyings. Even after 1000 cycles, the 3D Bi-nanonetworks surrounded by the HC matrixes are well maintained.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0026_R_d62918568e936" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Adv. Mater.">26</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0029_R_d62918568e936" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - J. Mater. Sci.">29</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0031_R_d62918568e936" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The well-interconnected Bi-nanonetworks and HC particles ensure continuous electron pathways and facilitate electrolyte infiltration, which effectively inhibits the detachment of active materials from the current collector (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0003">3j</a>).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202412636-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/cba28c7b-8a96-497a-b106-09231c6e2498/adma202412636-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/cba28c7b-8a96-497a-b106-09231c6e2498/adma202412636-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/cb5da04f-5554-46a0-bbeb-670be1c07936/adma202412636-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/cba28c7b-8a96-497a-b106-09231c6e2498/adma202412636-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202412636-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202412636" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The cycling performance and morphology evolutions of µm-Bi surrounded by µm-HC particles. a) Cycling performance of the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> thick-film electrode, delivering no capacity loss after 1000 cycles. The corresponding cross-sectional SEM images of Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> thick-film electrodes at b,c) pristine state, d,e) after 1 cycle, f,g) after 10 cycles, h,i) after 500 cycles, and j,k) after 1000 cycles, respectively. l) In situ XRD pattern of the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> electrode at 0.15 A g<sup>−1</sup>. m) In situ optical microscopy images of the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> electrode at selected (de)sodiation points, displaying a gentle volume expansion of 85.8% at the fully sodiated state.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>According to in situ XRD results (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0003">3l</a>), the initial sodiation curve of Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> is divided into four regions: the sloping curve in 1.5–0.1 V vs. Na<sup>+</sup>/Na from the “adsorption” sodiation of HC, the plateau at ≈0.6 V refers to Bi→NaBi, the plateau at 0.4 V refers to NaBi→Na<sub>3</sub>Bi, and the region in 0.01–0.10 V from the “intercalation-filling” sodiation of HC. The desodiation process is highly reversible. In situ optical microscopy is also employed to record the volume expansions of the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> thick-film electrode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0003">3m</a>; Video <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information). The corresponding volume expansions for the above four steps are 4.7%, 17%, 84.7%, and 85.8%, respectively. Since the HC electrode has negligible volume changes during (de)sodiation (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>; Video <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information), the volume expansion for the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> electrode is from Na–Bi alloying reaction. Importantly, compared to the irregular expansion of the µm-Bi electrode (Video <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information), the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> electrode exhibits uniform expansion (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0003">3m</a>).</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202412636-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adma202412636-sec-0050-title">2.3 Comprehensive Electrochemical Performance of µm-Bi/HC Electrode</h3>
            
            <p>Fine controls of the Bi:HC mass ratios are adopted. The µm-Bi particles are uniformly dispersed around the µm-HC particles, as demonstrated by ex situ SEM images and energy dispersive spectroscopy (EDS) mappings (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information). Additionally, with increasing Bi content, the compaction densities of the µm-Bi/HC composites are significantly enlarged than that of pure HC particles (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information). <b>Table</b> <a class="tableLink scrollableLink" title="Link to table" href="#adma202412636-tbl-0001">1</a> shows the compaction densities of the electrodes, calculated based on the cross-sectional SEM images (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a>, Supporting Information).</p>

               <div class="article-section__table-source"></div>

            <p>The capacity vs. potential profiles of the µm-Bi/HC composite thick-film electrode during the initial two cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> are plotted in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202412636-fig-0004">4a</a>. The related specific and volumetric capacities are listed in Table&nbsp;<a class="tableLink scrollableLink" title="Link to table" href="#adma202412636-tbl-0001">1</a>. Notably, the ICEs associated with various composite materials all exceed 87.8%, surpassing those of previously reported Bi and Bi/C composite anodes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0019_R_d62918568e1316" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - J. Energy Chem">19</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0020_R_d62918568e1316" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Energy Environ. Sci">20</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0024_R_d62918568e1316" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Mater.">24</a>-<a href="#adma202412636-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0031_R_d62918568e1316" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The presence of three distinct plateaus at 0.66, 0.5, and 0.05 V vs. Na<sup>+</sup>/Na indicates that the capacity of the composite material is contingent upon the relative content of Bi and HC.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0040_R_d62918568e1324" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Batteries Supercaps">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> electrode demonstrates a reversible areal capacity of 1.77 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Most importantly, compared with the µm-Bi electrode, the hybrid µm-Bi/HC thick-film electrodes deliver significantly improved cycling stability (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0004">4b</a>). After 2000 cycles, the capacity retentions of HC (100%), Bi<sub>20</sub>HC<sub>80</sub> (100%), and Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> (99.8%) are superior to those of Bi<sub>60</sub>HC<sub>40</sub> (94.2%), Bi<sub>80</sub>HC<sub>20</sub> (22.8%), and µm-Bi (7.5%). The volume expansion of the electrodes are calculated by in situ optical microscopy (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a>, Supporting Information). The Bi<sub>60</sub>HC<sub>40</sub> (Video <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information) and Bi<sub>80</sub>HC<sub>20</sub> (Video <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information) electrodes display large volume expansion of 178% and 320%, higher than that of 85.8% for Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> (Video <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information) and 67.4% for Bi<sub>20</sub>HC<sub>80</sub> (Video <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information). Therefore, attributing to the insufficient contents of HC for effectively separating the µm-Bi particles with adequate buffering zones (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a>, Supporting Information), the Bi<sub>80</sub>HC<sub>20</sub> and Bi<sub>60</sub>HC<sub>40</sub> electrodes show unsatisfactory cycling stabilities. Additionally, the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> and Bi<sub>20</sub>HC<sub>80</sub> electrodes show excellent cycling performance, with capacity retentions of 98.5% and 100%, respectively, after 5000 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information). These results indicate the crucial importance of an appropriate Bi:HC ratio in supporting ultralong cyclability and high capacity.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202412636-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/579e9385-55bb-4895-af5c-f4057f04e073/adma202412636-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/579e9385-55bb-4895-af5c-f4057f04e073/adma202412636-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/cb3d130b-d77a-4cc9-a596-64321b46e465/adma202412636-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/579e9385-55bb-4895-af5c-f4057f04e073/adma202412636-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202412636-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202412636" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance of the hybrid µm-Bi/HC electrodes. a) Galvanostatic discharge/charge curves of Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes during the initial two cycles. b) Cycling performance of the Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. c) CV curves of the Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes at a sweep rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>−1</sup>. d) Rate performance of Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes and the corresponding specific capacity contributions from Bi and HC. e) Volumetric capacities of Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes at various currents. f) Radar charts of the comprehensive electrochemical performance of the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>, µm-HC, and µm-Bi thick-film electrodes.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves of the Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes at 0.1 mV s<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0004">4c</a>) exhibit the related cathodic and anodic peaks of A<sub>1</sub>/A<sub>2</sub> for Bi↔NaBi, B<sub>1</sub>/B<sub>2</sub> for NaBi↔Na<sub>3</sub>Bi, and C<sub>1</sub>/C<sub>2</sub> for the intercalation-filling process for HC. The potential gap (Δ<i>E</i>) between the cathodic and anodic peaks of A<sub>1</sub>/A<sub>2</sub> and B<sub>1</sub>/B<sub>2</sub> as a function of Bi content was calculated (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a>, Supporting Information). With increasing Bi content, Δ<i>E</i> greatly enlarges owing to the limited mass transport kinetics on the higher percentages of Bi. Additionally, the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was employed for the kinetics analysis (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a>, Supporting Information). For the Bi/HC composite, the interconnected Bi-nanonetworks provide pathways of electron and infiltration of electrolyte, resulting in boosted reaction kinetics.</p>
            
            <p>The rate capacities of the Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes were further measured (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a>, Supporting Information). The detailed capacity contributions from the HC and Bi in the Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0004">4d</a>) are calculated from their charge–discharge curves at different specific currents (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a>, Supporting Information). At low currents (&lt;1 A g<sup>−1</sup>), the Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes align well with the calculated capacity contributions from the percentage composition of the pure µm-HC and µm-Bi electrodes (the dashed line in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0004">4d</a>). Remarkably, at currents over 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the µm-HC and µm-Bi electrodes display poor rate performance, but the specific capacities of Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> (20≤&nbsp;<i>x</i>&nbsp;≤80) are higher than the dashed line, which indicates a significantly enhanced rate capability of the hybrid design. The boosted rate capabilities are attributed to the increased contribution from the Na-Bi alloying reactions at high currents (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a>, Supporting Information), owing to the continuous electron transport by the in situ formed HC/Bi-nanonetworks with reduced overpotentials. Ex situ Raman spectra of the cycled µm-Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> electrodes (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a>, Supporting Information) do not show the formation of chemical bonds between Bi and C, indicating the enhanced electrochemical performance largely relayed on the robust physical contact between the electrochemically-formed Bi-nanonetworks and stable HC particles.</p>
            
            <p>The volumetric capacities of the Bi<i><sub>x</sub></i>/HC<sub>100−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i> thick-film electrodes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0004">4e</a>) at different currents are further calculated. Benefiting from the increase in compaction density due to the addition of µm-Bi, the Bi<sub>20</sub>HC<sub>80</sub>, Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>, Bi<sub>60</sub>HC<sub>40</sub>, and Bi<sub>80</sub>HC<sub>20</sub> deliver the volumetric capacities of 303, 422, 595, and 956 mAh cm<sup>−3</sup>, respectively, which are higher than that of the HC electrode (279 mAh cm<sup>−3</sup>). Notably, at high currents, the volumetric capacities of the µm-Bi/HC electrode far exceed those of the HC electrode. The overall performances of the µm-Bi/HC electrodes are summarized in the radar charts (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0004">4f</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a>, Supporting Information), demonstrating that the coupling of µm-Bi and HC enhances comprehensive electrochemical properties. The Bi<sub>40</sub>H<sub>60</sub> electrode offers the best balance among high ICE, high specific/volumetric capacity, high rate capability, and excellent cycling stability. The “root-growth-inspired” design is applicable to other alloying-type anodes. For example, the Sn/HC thick-film electrode shows much enhanced cycling performance compared to that of the pure Sn electrode as well (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <p>Above all, the root-growth-inspired design unitizes the expansion and morphology evolution of the alloy-type materials during cycling, displaying the following advantages (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0005">5</a>). 1) The electrochemical evolution from µm-Bi to porous Bi-nanonetworks makes full use of the voids between stacked HC particles, which reduces the volume changes and boosts the structural stability of thick-film electrodes during repeated (de)alloying reactions. 2) The electrochemically in situ formed Bi-nanonetworks are separated by HC particles, guaranteeing continuous electron pathways and preventing the loss of electric contact. 3) The distributed Bi-nanonetworks act as reservoirs, facilitating electrolyte permeation and Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion. 4) Both Bi and HC are electrochemically active, thus their specific and volumetric capacities are not sacrificed. 5) Microsized particles deliver high ICEs and economic effectiveness for commercial applications.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202412636-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/76bc4bfd-408a-43ca-9b11-c89eeb9e199f/adma202412636-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/76bc4bfd-408a-43ca-9b11-c89eeb9e199f/adma202412636-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/94852c51-1343-4202-ba8e-3800078e4e2c/adma202412636-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/76bc4bfd-408a-43ca-9b11-c89eeb9e199f/adma202412636-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202412636-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202412636" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Schematic of the “root-growth-inspired” self-morphology-evolution of µm-Bi cycling surrounded by µm-HC particles for boosted comprehensive sodium-ion storage performance.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202412636-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adma202412636-sec-0060-title">2.4 Electrochemical Performance of Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> Full Cell</h3>
            
            <p>A full cell consisting of a Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> anode and a Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) cathode was assembled (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202412636-fig-0006">6a</a>) without additional pre-treatment. The NVP cathode delivers an excellent high-rate capability (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0041_R_d62918568e1726" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Energy Mater.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The electrochemical performance of the full cell was measured in 1.9–3.4 V, and the capacity and energy density were calculated based on the total mass of cathode and anode materials. The first charge and discharge curves indicate an ICE of 80.1% at 0.2 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a>, Supporting Information), with a reversible capacity of 81 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>. Furthermore, the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||NVP full cell delivers better rate performance than the Bi||NVP cell (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0006">6b</a>). The Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||NVP full cell delivers capacities of 74, 53, and 26 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 1, 8, and 20 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>, corresponding to (dis)charging times of 44, 4, and 0.5 min, respectively. The charge and discharge curves of the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||NVP full cell (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0006">6c</a>) show reversible plateaus owing to the superior rate capability of Bi<sub>40</sub>H<sub>60</sub> compared with that of µm-Bi (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202412636-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/c678485d-323f-4f70-a72e-35594b014d08/adma202412636-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/c678485d-323f-4f70-a72e-35594b014d08/adma202412636-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/a71146e4-337d-4e85-8cc4-e2dd9248cb4e/adma202412636-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/c678485d-323f-4f70-a72e-35594b014d08/adma202412636-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202412636-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202412636" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance of the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> full cell. a) Schematic of the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||NVP full cell. b) Rate performance of Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||NVP and Bi||NVP full cells. The capacity is calculated by the total mass of the cathode and anode. c) Charge–discharge curves of Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||NVP cells at various current densities. d) Cycling performance of Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||NVP and Bi||NVP cells at 4 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>. e) Ragone plots of Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||NVP cell and previously reported results.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0043" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0043_R_d62918568e1827" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">43</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0048" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0048_R_d62918568e1827" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv. Mater.">48</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0050" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0050_R_d62918568e1827" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small">50</a>-<a href="#adma202412636-bib-0055" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0055_R_d62918568e1827" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - J. Mater. Chem. A">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub> also has long-term durability in full cells, while the morphological evolution of µm-Bi (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30</a>, Supporting Information) is consistent with half-cell observation. After 4,500 cycles at 4 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>, the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||NVP cell retains a reversible capacity of 52 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, corresponding to a capacity retention of 83.9% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0006">6d</a>), which is much more stable than that of the Bi||NVP cell (capacity retention of 19.4% after 860 cycles) and previously reported results even with electrochemically pre-cycled treatments (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0024_R_d62918568e1856" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Mater.">24</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0028_R_d62918568e1856" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - J. Mater. Chem. A">28</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0042_R_d62918568e1856" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Adv. Energy Mater.">42</a>-<a href="#adma202412636-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0050_R_d62918568e1856" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Ragone plots of the Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||NVP cell demonstrate the combination of high energy and power densities, delivering energy densities of 223 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 82 W kg<sup>−1</sup> and 51 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 6480 W kg<sup>−1</sup>, which are better than those of previously reported state-of-the-art SIBs (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202412636-fig-0006">6e</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202412636-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0043_R_d62918568e1878" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">43</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0048_R_d62918568e1878" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv. Mater.">48</a>, <a href="#adma202412636-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0050_R_d62918568e1878" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small">50</a>-<a href="#adma202412636-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202412636-bib-0055_R_d62918568e1878" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - J. Mater. Chem. A">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202412636-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202412636-sec-0070-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>Scrutinizing the morphological evolution of microsized Bi particles during repeated Bi-Na (de)alloying, the failure mechanism of the µm-Bi thick-film electrode involves significant volume changes, leading to the loss of effective electrical contacts from current collectors. In this work, inspired by the process of “root growths in soils”, we prepare the hybrid µm-Bi/µm-HC thick-film electrodes with excellent cycling stability at high mass loadings. The optimal Bi<sub>40</sub>/HC<sub>60</sub> (in weight) thick-film electrode delivers comprehensive sodium-ion storage performance, including a high specific/volumetric capacity of 321 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>/463 mAh cm<sup>−3</sup>, a high ICE of 88.2%, 2000 stable cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> with negligible capacity loss, and high-rate capability. A capacity retention of 83.9% and stable voltage profiles are obtained for the as-assembled Bi<sub>40</sub>HC<sub>60</sub>||NVP full cell. These promising properties of the µm-Bi/µm-HC electrodes suggest the potential application in SIBs with long lifespans and high energy and power densities. Our work highlights the “root-growth-inspired” ideas of using the electrochemical morphology evolution of alloying-type materials for boosted electrochemical performance.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
